Client(ClientMixin, RequestFactory):\\n1029:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n1030:     A class that can act as a client for testing purposes.\\n1031: \\n1032:     It allows the user to compose GET and POST requests, and\\n1033:     obtain the response that the server gave to those requests.\\n1034:     The server Response objects are annotated with the details\\n1035:     of the contexts and templates Client(ClientMixin, RequestFactory):\\n1029:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n1030:     A class that can act as a client for testing purposes.\\n1031: \\n1032:     It allows the user to compose GET and POST requests, and\\n1033:     obtain the response that the server gave to those requests.\\n1034:     The server Response objects are annotated with the details\\n1035:     of the contexts and templates that were rendered during the\\n1036:     process of serving the request.\\n1037: \\n1038:     Client objects are stateful - they will retain cookie (and\\n1039:     thus session) details for the lifetime of the Client instance.\\n1040: \\n1041:     This is not intended as a replacement for Twill/Selenium or\\n1042:     the like - it is here to allow testing against the\\n1043:     contexts and templates produced by a view, rather than the\\n1044:     HTML rendered to the end-user.\\n1045:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n1046: \\n1047:     def __init__(\\n1048:         self,\\n1049: ):\\n1056:         super().__init__(headers=headers, query_params=query_params, **defaults)\\n1057:         self.handler = ClientHandler(enforce_csrf_checks)\\n1058: **request):\\n1064:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n1065:         Make a generic request. Compose the environment dictionary and pass\\n1066:         to the handler, return the result of the handler. Assume defaults for\\n1067:         the query environment, which can be overridden using the arguments to\\n1068:         the request.\\n1069:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n1070:         environ = self._base_environ(**request)\\n1071: \\n1072:         # Curry a data dictionary into an instance of the template renderer\\n1073:         # callback function.\\n1074:         data = {}\\n1075:         on_template_render = partial(store_rendered_templates, data)\\n1076:         signal_uid = \\\"template-render-%s\\\" % id(request)\\n1077:         signals.template_rendered.connect(on_template_render, dispatch_uid=signal_uid)\\n1078:         # Capture exceptions created by the handler.\\n1079:         exception_uid = \\\"request-exception-%s\\\" % id(request)\\n1080:         got_request_exception.connect(self.store_exc_info, dispatch_uid=exception_uid)\\n1081:         try:\\n1082:             response = self.handler(environ)\\n1083:         finally:\\n1084:             signals.template_rendered.disconnect(dispatch_uid=signal_uid)\\n1085:             got_request_exception.disconnect(dispatch_uid=exception_uid)\\n1086:         # Check for signaled exceptions.\\n1087:         self.check_exception(response)\\n1088:         # Save the client and request that stimulated the response.\\n1089:         response.client = self\\n1090:         response.request = request\\n1091:         # Add any rendered template detail to the response.\\n1092:         response.templates = data.get(\\\"templates\\\", [])\\n1093:         response.context = data.get(\\\"context\\\")\\n1094:         response.json = partial(self._parse_json, response)\\n1095:         # Attach the ResolverMatch instance to the response.\\n1096:         urlconf = getattr(response.wsgi_request, \\\"urlconf\\\", None)\\n1097:         response.resolver_match = SimpleLazyObject(\\n1098:             lambda: resolve(request[\\\"PATH_INFO\\\"], urlconf=urlconf),\\n1099:         )\\n1100:         # Flatten a single context.
